    <li> Argan oil is produced from the kernels of the argan tree (argania spinosa) and is found exclusively in morocco. It is the rarest and most expensive oil on earth and is used mainly to moisturise hair, skin, nails, face and body.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Received for review the product is presented in a 120mL brown glass bottle and comes with a capped pump action spray. It is colourless, relatively runny and has a pleasant mild nutty odour. It is very fast absorbing and leaves a thin shiny layer of oil on your skin after it has been applied.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Application of the product is done differently for each body region, however in general it involves using only 1-3 drops per application and it is likely to be more effective if used every 1-2 days:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hair-&lt;br /&gt;Apply 1-3 drops to the scalp or hair of washed hair and massage the oil in gently. Leave on hair for 30 mins.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Skin-&lt;br /&gt;Apply 1-3 drops to a washed face and massage into skin in a circular motion.     <li> Now, many people say this stuff is amazing/clears acne/heals scars/raises your grandmother back from the dead.This is the REAL stuff...now whether it works &#x27;wonders&#x27; for you, or just suffices as a moisturizer, may be up to your individually. Argan oil is supposed to be non-comedogenic (not supposed to clog your pores), so supposedly is unlikely to cause a breakout or clog pores. From my own experience, it has not caused any breakouts (I&#x27;ve had quite a while of use--by a different brand at first, bought at Whole Foods for quite a bit more money). I believe this is also the real stuff as the consistency, color, and slight odor are the same as the type sold in the aforementioned store. It has a slight odor--not &#x27;fishy&#x27;, not unless you&#x27;ve had some strange experiences with cod liver oil, though.&lt;br /&gt;As for its supposed miracles... one can often read that this is practically magic, like &#x27;women of Morocco use it&#x27;. Careful with statements like that--are the women of Morocco the most beautiful in the world with perfect skin? That has about as much meaning as saying &#x27;women of the U.S. use it&#x27;, and telling you to buy foot cream.  FYI, not hating on Moroccan women--just giving an example. Just because supposedly another nation may traditionally use a specific product doesn&#x27;t mean that product is the very best of the best.&lt;br /&gt;For me, it&#x27;s been decent...nothing too special. It does moisturize my face, but leaves it looking OILY, so I put it on at night after a face wash, and in the morning first thing out of the shower (quite a bit before putting on make-up). And I do NOT have oily skin--it is sensitive, but normal (neither dry, nor oily, nor with a t-spot). Great at night after washing the face...great as a make-up remover that can get that eye makeup off without hurting those with sensitive skin. Removes super long-lasting lipsticks easily. Leaves lips moisturized. However, you know what else can do that? More than a few other oils. Sweet almond oil has a slightly higher possibility of clogged pores than Argan oil, however I&#x27;ve used that as well (for about ten bucks for eight ounces). Then there&#x27;s more expensive stuff, etc, etc. About using it on nails/hair/etc... you get the result of a good oil; you do not get access to the fountain of life and your choice of princess crown.&lt;br /&gt;BOTTOM LINE: Buy the stuff if the Amazon price is within your price point and you want to try it; at this price, the 4oz makes as much sense as a small portion (especially since you can also use it as a body oil, etc). If you don&#x27;t like it on your face, and it doesn&#x27;t perform magic tricks for your nails or hair, at least it&#x27;s a good body oil that you can use up.</li>

    <li> There are an overwhelming selection of products available for skin care, therefore it can be very difficult to know which products are best if you want healthy, glowing skin. Two products which are currently gaining favor among natural skin care enthusiasts are rosehip oil and argan oil. The nuts of the argan tree are predominantly harvested in Morocco. Although argan oil is a relatively new and unfamiliar beauty product in the United States, it has actually been a skin care staple for many generations of Mediterranean women.&lt;br /&gt;As many people will know, rosehips are small fruits produced by a certain type of rose. Like argan oil, rosehip is very high in essential fatty acids. These have two benefits when applied to the skin.</li>
